\[
f(A)= -0.1899774242\,A^2+\frac{0.4598748748\,A^2}{0.7497988950\,A^4+1}.

Equivalently,
\[
f(A)=\frac{-0.1899774242\cdot 0.7497988950\,A^6 + (0.4598748748-0.1899774242)\,A^2}{0.7497988950\,A^4+1},
\]
so it has the structural form \(\dfrac{\alpha A^6+\beta A^2}{\gamma A^4+1}\) with fixed \(\gamma=0.7497988950\), and no constant term, no odd powers, no logs/exp/sin/cos, and no \(|A|\) kinks (but \(|A|^{2k}=A^{2k}\) is fine).

Below, each candidate is checked for whether its free constants can make it exactly this function for all (t,A).

### 1
Has \(A\), \(t\)-dependent term, and \(\log(1+\exp(\cdot))\). To match GT (no t, no log/exp), would need to zero out those parts: set \(c2=0, c5=0\). Then becomes \(A^2c0+Ac1+c4\). GT has no \(A\) or constant term ⇒ \(c1=0,c4=0\). Leaves \(A^2c0\), cannot match GT’s rational term. **No.**

### 6
Has terms with denominator \(c1+|A|^4\) plus an exp(sin(...t...)) term. To remove t dependence set \(c3=0\). Remaining:
\[

\]
This is promising: if we set \(c1=1/\gamma\) and scale numerator, we can match \(\dfrac{\alpha A^6+\beta A^2}{\gamma A^4+1}\) because
\[
\frac{c0A^2+c2A^6}{c1+A^4}=\frac{(c0/c1)A^2+(c2/c1)A^6}{1+(1/c1)A^4}.
\]
Choose \(1/c1=\gamma=0.7497988950\Rightarrow c1=1/\gamma\). Then choose \(c0/c1=\beta\) and \(c2/c1=\alpha\) where \(\alpha=-0.1899774242\cdot 0.7497988950\) and \(\beta=0.4598748748-0.1899774242\).
All are real, so feasible. Also \(|A|^{2,6}=A^{2,6}\) so exact equality for all real A. **Yes, matches.**
